Italy Invades Ethiopia: Mobilizing 14 Divisions, 300,000 Troops 65

Merchant ships transport soldiers back and forth 400 times, military organization is precise and complete, and expenses are not small. The House of Representatives Military Committee recently submitted a report on the army budget, which revealed the organization of the Italian-Ethiopian War. It is quite interesting. It is said that the total number of troops sent from Italy to East Africa is seven infantry divisions, one mountain division, and six Blackshirt divisions, totaling 300,000 men. In the country, another seven infantry divisions have been formed so that the main force will not be weakened by the Italian-Ethiopian War. As of February 1 this year, the total number of workers hired in East Africa was 60,000, used to build roads and other industries in order to penetrate the enemy territory. The above numbers do not include native soldiers and workers. Regarding health affairs, there are currently 120 ambulance teams serving on the front lines. The quartermaster department has sent countless food, wine, and various drinks to the front lines. 15,837,000 meters of yellow canvas for military uniforms were used, and 19,389,974 meters of other fabrics were used. The telephone lines laid by the engineering team are 1,892 kilometers long, using 5,501 telephones. 108 radio stations and 799 chemical test rooms were built. The barbed wire used on the front lines weighed 12,497 tons. In terms of transportation, Eritrea and Somaliland currently have 87,000 horses and mules and 11,000 trucks. Italian merchant ships carrying soldiers and military supplies to East Africa travel back and forth 400 times, not including the number of trips to transport military equipment. In short, the organization of this East African war is precise and complete, and can be called the ultimate. (Havas, 22nd)

Tokyo: The Army Main Affairs Bureau is organizing the implementation budget and additional budget for the eleventh year. The additional budget includes 183.04 million yuan for the Manchurian Incident, 20.04 million yuan for the improvement of armaments, 55 million yuan for the preparation of materials, and 7.58 million yuan for general new projects, totaling 270 million yuan. Therefore, the budget for the eleventh year may not have swelled much, but the army will start from the twelfth year to rush to enrich national defense, realize: enrich firepower equipment, newly establish mechanized equipment corps, expand aviation and air defense equipment, and increase troops. Japan has 350,000 tons of auxiliary ships, the United States has 270,000 tons, and the United Kingdom has 390,000 tons. However, the United States is scheduled to complete the ship construction plan within the treaty-allowed amount in Showa 16, so if the status quo is not maintained, the Empire will be at a significant disadvantage and a major defect will occur. Youth and Society (Part 1) 96

Society has always given youth many titles, such as "the backbone of society," "the bulwark of the nation," and "the future masters of the country," etc., which shows that society attaches great importance to youth. However, whether youth are truly the backbone of society, the bulwark of the nation, and the future masters of the country depends on whether youth can establish their ambitions and take on the responsibilities of society. If youth can establish their ambitions and take on their responsibilities, then they will be worthy of these titles; otherwise, they will fail to live up to society's expectations of youth.

I will now explain, from a sociological standpoint, the importance of youth's position in society, the responsibilities that youth should bear towards society, and the cultivation that youth should possess. I intend to make youth aware of the importance of their position, the magnitude of their responsibilities, and what preparations they should make to undertake the future endeavors of the nation and society.

The Importance of Youth's Position in Society: The importance of youth's position in society can be observed from three aspects:

First, youth are the most hopeful elements in society. We must know that youth is the most important period of life, and the foundation for all of life's endeavors is laid during this period. The great careers of great individuals all begin in their youth. This is in terms of an individual's life. If we look at it from the perspective of society, all of society's endeavors are waiting for youth to undertake them. It can be said that the entire educational process is precisely to cultivate youth to undertake all of society's endeavors. Therefore, youth are truly the most hopeful people in society. Society's emphasis on youth and its eager expectations of youth are precisely for this reason. We all know that older and middle-aged people have either already undertaken endeavors in society or are currently undertaking endeavors in society; their hopes have either already been realized or are being gradually realized; their achievements have already given society a considerable impression. For example, the great thoughts and great careers of great leaders have already made society admire and respect them. As for ordinary people, who toil all their lives, they have already disappointed society. Only the future endeavors of young people can be said to be "just beginning," giving society endless hope. Liang Qichao once compared the differences in the personalities of the old and the young in his essay "On Young China" to illustrate the greatness of young people's hopes. He said, "The old often think of the past, while the young often think of the future; because they think of the past, they have a lingering heart; because they think of the future, they have a hopeful heart; because they are nostalgic, they are conservative; because they are hopeful, they are enterprising; because they are conservative, they are forever old; because they are enterprising, they are new every day." His description of the elderly may be somewhat exaggerated, but his description of the hopeful and enterprising character of young people seems quite accurate. Confucius said, "The younger generation is to be regarded with awe; how do you know that those who come after will not be as good as we are?" This also says that young people have the greatest hope, so their future achievements are immeasurable. In short, there is no doubt that young people are the most hopeful elements in society.

Second, youth are the linchpin of cultural succession in society. We must know that society is continuous and that the members of society are constantly undergoing metabolism. And young people, in the middle of this metabolism, are the linchpin that connects the past and the future. On the one hand, they inherit all the cultural relics, systems, thoughts, and customs of the past society; on the other hand, they pass on all the modern cultural relics, systems, thoughts, and customs to future generations. The reason why society can continue to evolve depends entirely on this role of connecting the past and the future, and youth are responsible for this role.

Third, youth are the driving force of social progress. Social progress depends on two basic elements: great individuals and excellent culture. The two are also mutually causal. Excellent culture is often invented and created by great individuals, and great individuals are often nurtured and cultivated by excellent culture. But in general, culture is ultimately created by humans, so great individuals are the most important basic element for social progress.

Looking at history, the achievements of all great individuals mostly originate in their youth. We will now examine the situations of the youth of various great individuals (such as great inventors, great scientists, great thinkers, great entrepreneurs, etc.) based on their deeds.

Great inventors' interest in invention mostly begins in their youth. Edison liked to study machines from a young age. His initial inventions of various electrical machines were made when he was only a teenager. He continued to study and continue to invent, and became a great inventor of the world. For example, Westinghouse invented the air brake at the age of only twenty-three. Nobel's invention of dynamite began when he was only twenty-one years old. Bell's invention of the telephone also began at the age of twenty-two; and his invention of the "yingfang jiusu" machine was when he was only fifteen years old. Henry Ford's love of researching machine inventions also began when he was a teenager. In short, the emergence of inventors' inventions may be early or late, but the motivation for their inventions mostly originates in their youth. This shows the importance of the relationship between youth and invention.

Great scientists' interest in scientific research also begins in their youth. Darwin, the founder of evolution, developed an interest in studying biology at the age of sixteen or seventeen. He initially experimented with chemistry with his brother, and then entered the University of Edinburgh at the age of sixteen, where he developed an interest in zoology and made many specimens himself. He made new discoveries of marine animals at the age of seventeen. Since then, his interest has grown stronger, and he eventually became a great scientist. Faraday's interest in studying chemistry began at the age of thirteen or fourteen. As an apprentice in a painting workshop, he liked to study books on chemistry, electricity, and other subjects. In his spare time, he often listened to scientific lectures. After that, he studied hard and eventually became a great scientist. Comte, the founder of sociology, had ideas for social reform at the age of ten, and his ideas progressed further when he followed Saint-Simon at the age of twenty. The outline of his great work "Positive Philosophy" was completed when he was twenty-two years old. Spencer's social thought was already established at the age of twenty. The content of his essay published at the age of twenty-three remained unchanged throughout his life. Adam Smith's great book on economics, "The Wealth of Nations," was initially collected when he was only twenty-one or two years old. In short, the scientific research of great scientists all begins in their youth.

The ideological gestation of great thinkers also takes place in their youth. Let us take a few famous scholars in our country since the Song Dynasty as examples. Zhu Xi, a Neo-Confucian scholar of the Southern Song Dynasty, passed the imperial examination at the age of eighteen and was appointed as the registrar of Tong'an. He immediately selected outstanding children in the county to lecture on the way of sages and sages to cultivate oneself and govern others. From then on, he studied the scriptures extensively, investigated principles, and achieved great Confucian status. Lu Jiuyuan, also known as Lu Xiangshan, was an extraordinary child since childhood. When reading the Four Books, he asked questions. He once said: The affairs within the universe are my own affairs; my own affairs are the affairs of the universe. He also said: The universe is my mind, and my mind is the universe. Since then, he has devoted himself to research and became a great Neo-Confucian scholar of the Southern Song Dynasty, as famous as Zhu Xi. Wang Yangming of the Ming Dynasty, named Shouren, discussed the way of sages with Lou Yi when he was eighteen, and he felt that saints could be learned and attained. It can be seen that great thinkers were extraordinary in their youth.

The beginning of great entrepreneurs' careers also takes place in their youth. Sun Yat-sen took it upon himself to liberate the Chinese nation from a young age. When he was studying at the Guangzhou Boji Medical School, he was only twenty years old, he was engaged in revolutionary movement. The great career of George Washington in the United States also began in his youth. When he began his military life, he was only twenty-two years old. Otto von Bismarck, the Iron Chancellor of Germany, was heroic from a young age. When he was studying at the Universities of Göttingen and Berlin, he took it upon himself to restore the nation. Mazzini, Garibaldi, and Cavour, patriots in Italy, were all outstanding young people. Mazzini joined the Carbonari party when he was only ten years old; he organized the "Young Italy Party" when he was only twenty-five years old. Garibaldi joined the Young Party and participated in the patriotic movement when he was only twenty-two or three years old. Cavour exhorted himself to revive the nation from a young age. This is in terms of historical figures. Even in terms of the current national leaders and world professional families in our country, many have shown their great abilities in their youth.

In short, the performance of the great abilities of all great individuals, whether they are inventors, scientists, thinkers, entrepreneurs, etc., is mostly in their youth. Therefore, the great achievements of great individuals are established in their youth. We know that great individuals are the most important basic element for social progress, so youth is the driving force of social progress. (To be continued)

Page 8

Details of Ambassador Cheng Tianfang's Presentation of Credentials in Germany 97

Berlin Correspondence: Dr. Cheng Tianfang, the first Ambassador of the Republic of China to Germany, presented his credentials and met with the German Head of State at 1:00 p.m. on February 27th. At 12:30 p.m. that day, the Director of Protocol of the German Foreign Ministry, the Deputy Director of Protocol, and the Counselor of the Embassy came to greet him. Ambassador Cheng, accompanied by embassy staff Tan Baoduan, Yao Dingchen, Qiu Changkang, and Chen Zehua, all dressed in diplomatic uniforms, proceeded to the German Presidential Palace. The Ambassador and the Director of Protocol rode in the German President's car, which was equipped with the Presidential flag. The remaining embassy staff rode in three cars provided by the German Foreign Ministry. They arrived at the Presidential Palace at 12:45 p.m. A line of guards presented arms and played a march on military drums. The Foreign Affairs Secretary of the Presidential Palace led them into the reception room. At 1:00 p.m. sharp, the Director of Protocol entered to announce the Ambassador's title. They were then led into the auditorium. The Ambassador bowed to the German Premier, who returned the courtesy in the same manner. The Ambassador then delivered the following eulogy:

Eulogy: "Mr. Premier, I, the undersigned, am honored to be appointed as the Ambassador Extraordinary and Plenipotentiary of the Republic of China to the German Reich by order of the Chairman of the National Government of the Republic of China. Today, I present to Your Excellency the Letter of Credence, and I feel extremely honored. I am also carrying the Letter of Recall of the former Minister Liu Chongjie. I would like to thank you on behalf of the Chinese government for the kind treatment extended to the former Minister Liu during his tenure in your country. I have always admired the spirit of perseverance and struggle of the German people, their triumph over the environment, and their achievements in politics, economy, science, and industry. It is a great pleasure in my life to be able to personally come to your country as the first ambassador of my country and to associate with the people of your country. The relations between our two countries have always been harmonious. In recent years, the economic and cultural relations between the two countries have become increasingly close. The upgrading of diplomatic envoys on both sides can be seen as a demonstration of mutual friendship. In the future, I will certainly perform my duties faithfully and promote the friendly relations between the two countries. I know that in carrying out this important mission, I will be able to obtain the support of Your Excellency the Premier and the government of your country. With sincere intentions, I wish Your Excellency the Premier good health and your country prosperity." After the eulogy, the Ambassador personally presented the Letter of Credence. After the German Head of State accepted it, he handed it over to the Foreign Minister, who then delivered the following reply:

Reply: "Mr. Ambassador, I am deeply honored to be able to personally receive from your hands the letter from the Chairman of the National Government of your country notifying the special appointment of Your Excellency as the Plenipotentiary Ambassador. At the same time, I accept the Letter of Recall of your predecessor, Minister Liu Chongjie. I also express my admiration for the remarkable achievements of Minister Liu in promoting the political, economic, and cultural relations between China and Germany. I am gratified to hear Your Excellency's approval of the German nation and its achievements in various fields. Germany attaches great importance to maintaining and enhancing the friendly relations that have always existed between China and Germany. The decision of both sides to upgrade diplomatic representatives to ambassadors is a symbol of this desire and is sufficient to express the friendship connecting our two countries. I am pleased to hear that Your Excellency, as the first Ambassador of the Republic of China to Germany, has the noble duty of promoting and expanding the various friendly relations between the two countries, and I dare to tell Your Excellency that the German government and I will always give Your Excellency full support. I am very grateful for the Ambassador's expression of friendly wishes to Germany and myself personally, and I express the same wishes to Your Excellency. In the name of Germany, I extend a sincere welcome to Your Excellency the Ambassador."

After the ceremony, they sat down and exchanged pleasantries briefly. The German Premier inquired about the well-being of Chairman Lin and President Chiang, and was very kind and amiable. At this time, the embassy staff were still waiting in the reception room. The German Head of State then stood up and entered the reception room, followed by the Ambassador. The embassy staff bowed to the German Head of State, and the Ambassador introduced them one by one and shook hands with them. The German Head of State and his entourage then withdrew, and the embassy staff bowed again. The protocol officer tapped the ground with the tip of his ceremonial staff to indicate that the ceremony was complete. At 1:30 p.m., Ambassador Cheng led the embassy staff out of the Presidential Palace and returned to the embassy in the same cars, accompanied by the Counselor and the Secretary of the Protocol Department.

The ceremonies for diplomatic envoys of various countries to meet with the Heads of State are different, but the German regulations are relatively simple. The ceremony for a Minister to meet is roughly the same as the ceremony for an Ambassador to meet. However, there is no welcoming ceremony for Ministers. Ministers must ride in their own cars and are not allowed to bring embassy staff to the audience. In special circumstances, one attendant may be brought along. The Presidential Palace guards present arms as a salute, but do not beat drums. This is the difference.

The evening newspapers published in Berlin that day and the various daily newspapers in Berlin and outside the city on the 28th all carried lengthy reports and photos of the audience, and several major newspapers published the Ambassador's resume and words of praise for the Ambassador. All sectors of German society attached great importance to the audience of the first Ambassador of our country.

Beiping East Station Corpse in a Box Case: The Truth Unveiled - A Love Triangle Between Master and Servant - The Culprit Escaped, Awaiting Arrest 98

Beiping Correspondence: The case of the abandoned corpse in a box at Beiping East Station last month, due to the horrific dismemberment and the elaborate design of the box, caused a sensation in the Tianjin and Beiping areas. Both cities' Chinese and foreign detectives, under orders to solve the case within a deadline, concentrated their efforts to bring the perpetrator to justice as soon as possible. The truth of the case has only recently been clarified, with the perpetrator and the vehicle used to transport the box being found successively. However, Wang, the mastermind behind the murder, has yet to be apprehended. The progress of the investigation and the details of the case are described below.

A Director's Household: A Wife and a Concubine

Zhang Shulin, a Beiping native, twenty-four years old, served as a male servant in the residence of You Chuan, a former regimental commander. Jia, from Jilin, due to financial difficulties, transferred to Wang Huayi's residence as a guard. Wang, originally from Henan, forty-two years old, is currently the director of a military supply depot. His home is located at No. 5 Tongfu Alley, Dengshikou, in this city. His legal wife, Xi, is also from Henan and the same age as Wang. His concubine, Wang Shujing (also known as Huizhen), is thirty-four years old. Before marrying Wang, she was a nurse at Xiehe Hospital, known for her beauty. She married Wang five years ago and has two sons, Ji Hua, five years old, and Shao Hua, four years old. The family lives together harmoniously.

Illicit Relations Between Master and Servant: Eyes Through the Window

Wang's residence consists of two courtyards, front and back. The Zeng family lives in the back courtyard, while Wang lives in the front. His wife, Xi, and the female servant live in the five southern rooms. The three northern rooms are for guests. Wang and his concubine, Wang Shujing, live in the two western ear rooms. The rickshaw puller and male servants live in the gatehouse. Five years ago, Wang Shujing fell ill and was cared for by the female servant, Liu Wang. One day, after delivering ginseng soup, she was lured by Wang into the living room for an illicit affair. Zhang Shulin, the guard, returned from outside with a letter. Finding the living room door locked, he peeked through the window and discovered the secret. Wang, seeing someone spying outside, asked who it was. Zhang Shulin, afraid to speak, retreated to the gatehouse and did not tell anyone.

A Love Triangle: The Servant is Murdered

Later that evening, Zhang negotiated with Liu Wang in the servants' quarters, saying that it was demeaning enough for women to be servants, but to also have affairs with the master was unacceptable. Liu Wang, who had feelings for Zhang, seized the opportunity to ask him not to reveal the secret, saying, "I will treat you the same way I treat the master." The two then became involved. Later, Wang Huayi asked Liu Wang what her husband was doing. Liu Wang replied that he was unemployed. Wang then said that he could have him come to Beiping and find him a job. Soon after, Liu responded to the call and came to Beiping from his hometown of Changping. Wang then sent Zhang Shulin to accompany him to Baoding, giving him secret instructions to shoot and kill Liu Wang's husband along the way. He then forged a letter to Beiping, saying that he had been introduced by Wang to be an adjutant in a certain regiment of a certain division of a certain army, instructing Liu Wang to serve the master with peace of mind. Zhang Shulin then returned to Beiping and made similar claims. Liu Wang believed him and continued to alternate between Wang and Zhang, while Wang Xi and Wang Shujing remained in the dark.

Mismatched Couples: Mutual Intent to Kill

One day, Wang Huayi went to Tianjin on business, instructing Zhang Shulin to monitor his concubine Wang Shujing's actions, as she was known to be promiscuous. Unexpectedly, Zhang became involved with Wang Shujing. Liu Wang, upon hearing this, became jealous but could do nothing. When Wang returned to Beiping, Liu Wang told him about Zhang Shulin and Wang Shujing's secret. Wang was furious and told Liu Wang that he would kill Zhang Shulin sooner or later to avenge himself. When Liu Wang was intimate with Zhang, she relayed Wang's words, telling him to be careful. Zhang also said, "It's better to strike first. I will kill Wang Huayi first." Liu Wang also told Wang Huayi about this, leading to mutual intentions of killing between the master and servant.

Abandoning Wang for Zhang: Master and Servant at Odds

Before the New Year, Wang Huayi wanted to dismiss Zhang Shulin. Liu Wang, upon hearing this, and being in love with Zhang, preemptively resigned and moved to the Fuhua Ju Congee Shop at No. 4 Shiba Banjie Hutong inside Fuchengmen (the shop owner, Wang Keda, is Liu Wang's cousin). She gave birth to a son in the back room last month (only two months old). Wang Huayi, however, could not forget Liu Wang and sent his nephew, Wang Junhua, to deliver a letter, instructing Liu Wang to find another house as a separate residence. But Liu ignored him and claimed that her son was fathered by Zhang Shulin. Wang Huayi became even more resentful of Zhang Shulin.

A Playful Remark: A Prophecy Fulfilled

On the first day of the lunar new year this year, Zhang Shulin stayed with Liu Wang for two days. On the third day, after eating dumplings, Zhang said he was going to visit Commander Jia's residence first, and then visit Director Wang. Liu Wang immediately said, "Don't go to Director Wang's residence again, because Director Wang is planning to harm you." Zhang laughed and said, "If I really don't come back, you can go to Commander Jia and ask him to avenge me." They both thought it was a joke and didn't take it seriously. The next morning, Zhang left and never returned. Liu Wang was puzzled. She could read, and when she saw the corpse description of the corpse in a box case at the East Station in the newspaper, it resembled Zhang Shulin. She was restless all night and went to the Jia residence at Sigenbai to inquire. Wang Shujing was present and said that Zhang Shulin had absconded after stealing property. Someone from the Jia residence then called Wang's residence, who said that Zhang had just left. They then sent someone to investigate, and the people at the residence claimed that Zhang had not returned for two or three days, but they found that Zhang's bedding was being used by the rickshaw puller, Cai Yongxiang.

Plotting to Kill the Servant: Dismembering the Corpse and Packing it in a Box

The above situation was heard by detectives. The detective team first summoned Liu Wang for questioning, followed by Li Liangjing, Wang Shujing, Wang Junhua, Cai Yongxiang, Tian Yongxiang, Zhang Jinfu, and seven others. After questioning, they learned that when Zhang Shulin went to Wang's residence on the fourth day of the lunar new year, the people in the residence said that the master was looking for him and that he had a letter to deliver to No. 31 Jiaolou Alley, Dongsibei (the house is Wang Huayi's property and is currently empty). Zhang Shulin took the letter and walked there, while Wang Huayi, along with the cook Li Liangjing and Li's friend Xi Sangyuan, went ahead by car. When Zhang knocked on the door, Li opened it. As Zhang walked to the steps of the northern upper room, Li took out a pistol and shot Zhang in the back of the head. Zhang fell to the ground. Xi immediately used a rope to strangle Zhang's head, and Li used a knife to cut off Zhang's head, arms, and legs. Xi then bought two boxes from Longfusi and packed Zhang's body parts for disposal at a later time.

The Main Culprit is Apprehended: The Instigator is at Large

As the weather was cold, Zhang's body parts, although packed in boxes for several days, had not yet decomposed. The instigator, Wang Huayi, meticulously planned and called the Xingji Automobile Company in Nanchizi and the Jingjin Automobile Company, each calling for a car to transport the boxes to the East Station for disposal in Tianjin. Li and Xi were each rewarded with twenty yuan. The two boxes were transported to the station, but due to the weight exceeding the limit, Wang Huayi abandoned the boxes and escaped, causing the sensation of the corpse in a box case. The detective team, based on the statements of various individuals, arrested the main culprit Li Liangjing near Baoding. The instigator, Wang Huayi, and the accomplice, Xi Sangyuan, are at large. In addition to continuing the pursuit, the team transferred the seven male and female suspects to the Detective Headquarters for interrogation at 2:00 PM on the 22nd. It was previously reported that Wang Huayi was the former president of the Liaoning Education Association, but this has been proven to be completely inaccurate. (22nd)

Song Zheyuan Returns to Baoding to Interrogate Hebei-Chahar County Magistrates - After a Four-Five Day Delay in Baoding, He Will Inspect Various Counties in Western and Southern Hebei 99

Baoding Correspondence: Hebei Provincial Chairman Song Zheyuan has been absent from the province for a long time due to presiding over important military and political affairs and diplomatic matters in the Beiping-Tianjin area. He is now taking advantage of the interrogation of county magistrates and plans to personally inspect the hardships of the people in southern Hebei and deploy military forces to prevent bandits. He returned to Baoding by special train at 11:00 AM on the 21st. Those who came to Baoding with Song included, in addition to Madam Song, Pan Yugui, Director of the Political Affairs Department of the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Committee, Yang Zhennan, Director of the Chahar Provincial Civil Affairs Department, Zhang Yunrong, Director of the Hebei Security Department, as well as Men Zhizhong, Liu Yufen, and over a hundred secretaries, attendants, and guards. Sixty county magistrates from the Hebei and Chahar provinces who were to be interrogated also came along. Baoding, having received news of Song's return to the province in advance, prepared a grand welcome. Military and political leaders and representatives of the gentry, business, and academic communities, such as Wan Fulin, Feng Zhanhai, Wei Lantian, Zhang Jiyong, Li Jinzao, Wang Jingru, and Jia Yuzhang, a total of over five hundred people, came to the station to welcome him. The station and the city of Baoding were heavily guarded. After Song got off the train, he went directly to the Provincial Government by car. He met with the directors and members of various departments in the Provincial Government to inquire about the situation of the provincial administration. At 6:00 PM, he left the government to return the visit to Wan Fulin and others. At 7:00 PM, he returned to the Provincial Government to discuss important provincial affairs with the directors of various departments. He returned to his residence in Dajinxian Hutong at around 11:00 PM to rest. Starting on the morning of the 22nd, he met with guests from all sides in the Provincial Government and summoned important staff from various departments to give instructions. In the afternoon, he read documents in the Provincial Government. Starting on the 23rd, he interrogated Hebei-Chahar county magistrates in the auditorium of the Baoding Normal School Affiliated Elementary School, stipulating that the interrogations would be held separately from 8:00 AM to 11:00 AM in the morning and from 2:00 PM to 6:00 PM in the afternoon, with instructions added. It is expected that he will stay in Baoding for four or five days before heading south from Baoding to inspect various counties in western and southern Hebei, with Zhang Yunrong, Director of the Hebei Security Department, and others accompanying him. The places that Song will inspect are the counties in western and southern Hebei, and he may go as far as Handan County. The purpose of this inspection is to learn about the hardships of the people and to inspect the local defense corps in various counties, and then reorganize them, eliminating all the old, weak, and disabled soldiers, so as to effectively protect the local area. As for the military defense against bandits in western Hebei, he also intends to make thorough arrangements at that time. The bandits in southern Hebei are lurking, and if they are not eliminated quickly, they will cause great harm to the local area in the future. Song has decided to personally instruct the county magistrates when he arrives in Renxian and Yaoshan counties, urging them to suppress the bandits and eliminate them. After inspecting the various counties under the jurisdiction of Damingdao in southern Hebei, he will return to the province, manage provincial affairs briefly, and then go to Beiping to preside over military and political affairs in Beiping. Song is very serious about interrogating the county magistrates of Hebei and Chahar. In addition to Song's personal inquiries, Pan Yugui, Director of the Political Affairs Department of the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Committee, Zhang Jiyong, Director of the Hebei Civil Affairs Department, Yang Zhennan, Director of the Chahar Provincial Civil Affairs Department, as well as Men Zhizhong, Liu Yufen, and others, take turns giving instructions, and the county magistrates record notes for future reference and application. The drafts of these instruction notes will be used as the county magistrates' written examinations, and graders will review them to understand the county magistrates' knowledge and thoughts. Those who are overly inferior will be replaced to avoid delaying local county administration. Pan Yugui came to Baoding specifically to handle this matter. Pan will leave Baoding and return to Beiping after the county magistrate interrogation is completed. (22nd)

Penang Correspondence: Mr. Li Changan, manager of the Wanbao Ginseng and Velvet Antler Bureau in Penang, has always had a great deal of research on ginseng and velvet antler, and has returned to China for investigation and procurement of large quantities of top-quality sika deer antler for many years. From left to right, the first person is Li Changan. The second person is Consul General Quan Shien. The third person is Deputy Consul.

Restrictions on Entry of Overseas Chinese in Various Parts of British Malaya - More Than 300 Overseas Chinese Blocked in Hong Kong 101

Xiamen Correspondence: Overseas Chinese in the Nanyang Islands are mostly from southern Fujian. The American-owned Philippines has extremely strict restrictions and no longer allows new arrivals. Although the Dutch-owned territories do not absolutely prohibit entry, the restrictions are extremely harsh. However, British-owned territories originally had no restrictions. In 1929, Nanyang was hit by a recession, and rubber plantations and tin mines successively shut down. Overseas Chinese lost their jobs. Since 1931, restrictions have also been imposed, but not as strict as those in Dutch-owned territories. After 1934, rubber plantations and tin mines in Nanyang gradually resumed operations. At the same time, the construction of the Singapore naval port required Chinese workers, and the number of immigrants gradually increased. Recently, the four ports of Hainan, Hong Kong, Shantou, and Xiamen have been limited to 3,000 people per month, with Xiamen accounting for 1,200 people. These 1,200 new passengers are distributed among the British-owned shipping companies, including 400 for Taikoo, 200 for Hetong, 200 for Yaga Company, 200 for Hefuqing's Jinma Wanfushi two ships, 150 for Jardine, and 50 for the Norwegian Haixing Haili two ships. Each shipping company sells new passenger tickets every month according to this quota. However, the various industries in southern Fujian are in recession, and the number of people trying to go abroad to make a living far exceeds 1,200. Shipping companies distribute the tickets within the quota to various inns and ticket agencies. Each ticket costs 61 yuan (third-class steerage). Because the supply and demand are too different, the inns and ticket agencies take advantage of the situation and raise prices, with each ticket rising to 120 yuan, and up to 160 yuan at the highest. Shipping companies, under pressure from public opinion, have limited the price that inns and ticket agencies can sell for to no more than 80 yuan. However, those who are eager to go abroad still often endure the pain and bid high prices to buy tickets. Currently, the publicly sold tickets cost more than 110 yuan, and some are actually sold for 140 to 150 yuan. Some poor passengers who are trying to go abroad have exhausted all their savings and still do not have enough to buy a ticket, so tragedies arise. On March 1, the "Meimei" cargo ship that departed from Hong Kong and arrived in Singapore on the 8th, British government officials strictly inspected the cargo hold because they were searching for smuggled opium. They inadvertently discovered 137 new passengers without permits at the bottom of the third-floor cargo hold (those who obtained tickets within the limit were issued entry permits by the shipping company on behalf of the British government, which is called having a permit). These passengers included 40 to 50 people from Guangdong, 56 from Chaozhou and Shantou, and 37 from Fuzhou. These new passengers were poor and penniless and could not afford a ticket. The inns took the opportunity to make a profit, transporting them to Hong Kong, colluding with people on the cargo ship, treating people as cargo, giving them 10 yuan per person for transportation, and closing them at the bottom of the third-floor cargo hold. After arriving in Singapore and unloading the cargo, they waited for an opportunity to let them ashore one after another. This method has been used for more than just one decision. Some were lucky enough to reach their destination, but many were suffocated to death in the bottom of the cabin, and their bodies were thrown into the sea when they sailed back to Hong Kong, which is also very tragic. Since Singapore discovered that new passengers were being smuggled as cargo, inspections have been strict. More than 300 poor new passengers from Fuzhou and Fuqing have been blocked in Hong Kong. (March 22)

Songjiang: The Hu Family Pond Doctor Robbed

Hu Zhenhua, a doctor in the Hu Family Pond, Xin Zhuang Town,

At 1:30 AM on the 21st, more than a dozen bandits suddenly arrived, speaking with local accents, holding pistols and flashlights. One thief climbed over the wall and entered, opening the main gate to lead the group inside to rob. After obtaining the loot, they split up and went to the home of Hu Desheng, who lived with them, to search and loot, heading east after plundering. The victim checked the lost property and found that Hu Zhenhua lost 110 yuan, three gold rings, and miscellaneous clothing and items worth several hundred yuan. The thief left behind a pistol bullet head. Hu Desheng's family lost 110 yuan in cash, 4 yuan in silver, and relatively few clothing and cloth items. The case has been reported to the Sixth Public Security Sub-station for investigation.

Suzhou: Bandits Discovered in East Taihu

Recently, more than 7,000 bandits suddenly poured into East Taihu from Zhejiang. The Wu County and Wujiang Public Security Bureaus have dispatched teams to strictly guard the key points on the lakeshore. It is now known that 60 bandits with weapons and red cloth wrapped around their arms have been discovered in Dianshan Lake, which has been peaceful for a long time. The Second District of the Waterborne Public Security Bureau has received a telegram from Wujiang County Magistrate Xu asking them to send a team to jointly suppress the bandits. At the same time, the Wu County Public Security Bureau arrested Wang Yinquan and Zhu Buhai, two members of the Big Sword Society who came to Suzhou from Liyang, in the Hongfu Tea House on Wanli Bridge on Damalu Road outside the Gate of Chang. Because the area is in the Jinghu Railway area, they were handed over to the Railway Police Department for questioning.

Wuxi: Two Robberies and Assaults in One Night - Recently, robberies have been frequent in the four rural areas of Wuxi. Yesterday, there were two more robberies in the Fifth and Eighth Districts, and both resulted in injuries to the victims. Details are recorded as follows: At the home of Fang Jinguan, a farmer in Chengtang Village, Fifth District, twelve bandits suddenly arrived the night before, all carrying weapons, and some wearing yellow coats. They broke into the house and robbed a small urn of cash and 16 yuan in paper money. Before leaving, they shot and wounded Fang Jinguan and left with a roar. In the Eighth District, Nan Chuanfang is adjacent to Baqu in Wu County. The night before, five bandit ships suddenly arrived, with more than 20 bandits on board. After landing, they first robbed the home of the farmer Xu Fubao, then robbed the home of his neighbor Xu Genfu, and beat Fubao and Genfu's wife, Chen, causing serious injuries. Before leaving, they fired shots to show their strength. The two families lost more than 100 yuan. Both cases have been reported to the county for injury verification and for requesting an investigation.

The Vehicle Industry Appeals for Exemption from Business Tax

The County Chamber of Commerce reported that the human-powered vehicle industry complained that it had been summoned and detained by the Public Security Bureau for failing to pay back taxes demanded by the Business Tax Bureau, and requested relief. It was found that the human-powered vehicle industry in Wuxi has been paying vehicle donations to the local government since the beginning of the business tax, which are calculated by vehicle and are small, but the amount is already large, and it is not convenient to impose additional burdens. Moreover, most of the industry is made up of poor people in the local area, and neighboring counties in Suzhou and Changzhou have not levied this tax. The Wuxi Business Tax Bureau has repeatedly demanded the payment of old debts, and the Public Security Bureau has also arrested and pursued the debts. Such oppression of small businesses and disregard for human rights is difficult to remain silent on. Yesterday, a letter was sent to the county government requesting that the Business Tax and Public Security Bureaus be ordered to stop demanding payment, and that the relevant parties should discuss and coordinate how to reduce the original local monthly donations and how to take into account both the monthly donation and the business tax, and that no further demands should be made until a solution is determined in order to alleviate the burden on small businesses and stabilize the local area.

Changzhou - Bandits Kidnap and Injure People in Yinanyi Township

Bandits Kidnap and Injure People in Yinanyi Township, Changzhou

Gu Fuyou, of Yinanyi Township in the Ninth District of Wujin, has a modest family fortune, which has attracted the attention of bandits. It happened that at about 8:00 PM on the 21st, more than 20 bandits suddenly arrived, armed with box guns and flashlights, and climbed over the wall into the inner room of Gu's house. They tied up and beat the victim, Gu Fuyou, and severely burned him with fire. They then rummaged through boxes and cabinets and looted at will for more than an hour. Gu's eldest son sneaked out and reported to the watch post in Five Lane Village. The watchman rushed to the scene to catch the bandits. Seeing that the situation was not good, the bandits fired shots and carried their loot away towards Yixing. Before leaving, they kidnapped Gu's 13-year-old second son. The report was later made by the Ninth District Office and the Eighth Public Security Sub-station, and District Chief Xue Youben and Patrol Officer Fang Dingli reported to the county government on the 12th and tried to rescue the hostage.

Mingguang: Agricultural Bank Loans 300,000 Yuan - Wu Jing, the Director-General of the Provincial Cooperative Committee, inspected Chuzhou some time ago. Considering that the county's cooperative organization was sound and the local government provided strong assistance, he telegraphed the head office of the China Farmers' Bank in Hankou to request a loan of 300,000 yuan, specifically for water conservancy and marketing matters. It is now learned that it has been approved and that Mr. Cheng Yongqing has been sent to handle all the formalities.

Yangzhou: Disputes Over Exorbitant Interest - Tao Songshan, a resident of Shaobo Town, Yangzhou, used a gold bracelet as collateral to Zhao Xunzhi for 170 yuan in the autumn of the 19th year of the Republic of China. A few days ago, he took the money and interest to redeem the bracelet, but Zhao Xunzhi demanded interest on interest, calculating at an exorbitant rate, demanding 600 yuan before he would return the bracelet. The Tao family believed that even if the five years of interest were calculated at 2%, the principal and interest would only be more than 300 yuan. As they could not agree, Zhao turned Tao Songshan and the broker Sun Zhulin over to the Yangzhou Public Security Bureau, and they were detained in the bureau for two days before being released. Tao Songshan, feeling wronged, has filed a lawsuit with the local court. It is said that Zhao Xunzhi's letter openly demanding 600 yuan from the Tao family has been attached to the petition.

Nantong: British Warships Conduct Shooting Exercises in Tong

Recently, foreign warships have been stationed in the Nantong Wolf Mountain River. On the 21st, a British warship with a red smokestack arrived. It conducted live ammunition shooting exercises outside the Xiaoyang Port. Gunfire and cannon fire continued from morning to noon. The ship was more than ten miles from the shore, and its name is unknown. It sailed to Shanghai in the evening.

Gaoyou: A Monk Cuts Off His Right Hand While Begging for Alms

A monk named Wei Xiu from the Emei Zhaoxian Temple outside the West Gate of Yangzhou came to Gaoyou to beg for alms to repair the temple. After begging for many days, no one donated. Last night, he went to the home of You Shaoqiu, a wealthy household in Xihe Lane in the city, to beg for 500 cash as travel expenses to return to Yangzhou. The You family not only refused, but also said that he was repairing his "Five Viscera Temple" (stomach) and that he should show some sincerity if he was truly cultivating his mind. Unexpectedly, this morning (the 20th) at 7:00 AM, Wei Xiu bought a kitchen knife and went to the front of You's house and slashed his right hand, causing blood to gush out and fainting on the ground. The whole city was shocked, and many people came to watch. Later, a Daoist woman reported to the Tieqiao Old Monk of the Shan Yin Temple outside Beidou, who came and carried him to the Huoxing Temple, and hired a doctor to treat him.

Bengbu: Counterfeit Currency Ring Cracked

After the newly cast copper-nickel alloy subsidiary coins arrived in Bengbu, they circulated on the market and were welcomed by merchants and the public. However, in recent days, many counterfeit metal-quality subsidiary coins suddenly appeared on the market. Citizens were easily deceived, and many suffered losses as a result. The local authorities paid close attention to this. After cracking a counterfeit money trafficking ring in Yuqingli in the First District, the Public Security Bureau received a tip that someone was secretly casting and selling metal-quality counterfeit subsidiary coins in private, using counterfeits to confuse the real coins in order to profit. Under strict investigation by the Public Security Bureau, they cracked the ring at Li Yitong's house in Gaoyingzi yesterday. They found many counterfeit coins, lead blocks, and molds, and sent Li and the evidence to the Public Security Bureau. The interrogation revealed that it was closely related to the counterfeit money manufacturing ring that was cracked the day before. The witnesses were transferred to the court for questioning.

Japanese Ambassador Arita Left Shanghai for Tianjin Yesterday 108

The Conference of Japanese Consuls in North China to Be Held Tomorrow; After the Conference, He Will Go to Changchun via Tianjin and Return to Japan via Korea

Japanese Ambassador to China, Hachiro Arita, returned to Shanghai from Nanjing a few days ago and immediately convened a conference of consuls general stationed in Nanjing, Shanghai, Jinan, Qingdao, Hankou, Fuzhou, Guangzhou and other places to listen to reports. Because Ambassador Arita urgently needed to return to Japan, he took a special train car provided by the Chinese and left Shanghai at 4 p.m. yesterday with his wife and secretary Kondo, heading north to Tianjin, going via the three Northeastern Provinces and returning to Japan via Korea. Details are as follows:

Japanese Consular Conference – No Report Issued 109

The second conference of Japanese Consuls General in China was held at the Japanese Consulate General on Wuchang Road yesterday, starting at 9:30 a.m. Ambassador Arita presided over the conference. Consuls General from various regions including Ishii (Shanghai), Suma (Nanjing), Miura (Hankou), Nishi (Qingdao), Kawai (Guangzhou), Nakamura (Fuzhou), and Nishida (Jinan) attended. Also present were embassy officials Waksugi, Horiuchi, Arino, Ashino, and Motono. The conference adjourned at 12 noon. The conference yesterday heard reports from Consuls General Kawai and Nakamura. The results of the two-day conference were originally scheduled to be formally released by the Japanese Consulate General yesterday afternoon, but this was temporarily cancelled. According to the Japanese side, the results of the conference have been taken back to Tokyo by Ambassador Arita for reporting. It is also understood that the consuls general of various regions, since the conference has ended, are scheduled to leave Shanghai today and tomorrow to return to their posts.

Passing Nanjing Without Stopping; Arriving in Tianjin Tonight 110

After the conference adjourned, Ambassador Arita returned to his residence on Bixun Road to rest and pack his luggage. Then, at about 3:30 p.m., he and his wife and others took several cars to the North Railway Station and boarded a special train car provided by the Chinese. At 4:00 p.m., he left for Tianjin, heading north. He does not intend to get off the train when passing Nanjing. He is scheduled to arrive in Tianjin on the evening of the 24th. He will stay in Tianjin for three days, presiding over the conference of consuls in North China on the 25th to hear reports. He will also meet with Japanese military attachés stationed in North China to listen to reports. After the matter is completed, he does not intend to go to Peiping. (According to New Sound News, Arita will meet with the commander of the Japanese garrison in China, Tada, after the conference, and then go to Peiping to personally inspect the affairs of the embassy on weekdays. He will also visit Song Zheyuan, chairman of the Hebei-Chahar Political Council, and others for a talk. He is scheduled to leave the customs on the 28th.) He will then go to Changchun via Tianjin to inspect the customs and conditions of the three Northeastern Provinces, and then return to Japan via Korea. He is scheduled to arrive in Tokyo in mid-April.

Zhejiang Opens Silk Cocoon Ban 114

The Province is Divided into Eight Districts to Ban Excess Cocoon Merchants from Purchasing; Allocated 160,000 Yuan for Improving Mechanical Loans

After the Zhejiang Provincial Sericulture Control Committee was established in Hangzhou on the 21st, members Shen Huachen, Zhu Jingan, and Chu Huiseng returned to Shanghai. A reporter from the New Sound News met with Shen Huachen and others yesterday and was informed of the proceedings of the control meeting, which are recorded as follows:

This Year's Opening of the Silk Cocoon Ban 115

After the reorganization of the Zhejiang Provincial Sericulture Control Committee, which is now directly under the Provincial Government, in addition to stipulating that the magistrates of the 32 counties should be ex officio members, Chu Huiseng and ten others were hired as members. A meeting was held in Hangzhou on the 21st to establish the committee. Provincial Chairman Huang Shaoxiong and former Finance Director Xu Qingfu attended. Chairman Zeng Yangfu decided on the spot that Zhejiang Province should be divided into eight districts, and a district office should be established in each district. The first step is for the district office to verify the cocoon banks in each district and submit them to the Control Committee for review. The second step is that any silk manufacturer who wants to collect cocoons should first apply for approval.

Banning Non-Silk Manufacturers 116

It is strictly stipulated that non-silk manufacturers may not apply to collect cocoons. The collection of cocoons by excess cocoon merchants is strictly prohibited. If anyone is found to be impersonating a factory, they will be severely punished. At the same time, it is stipulated that the standard for cocoon bank baking is 3.4 yuan per dan, but it should not be lower than 2.4 yuan per dan. Any silk factory merchant who wants to go to various districts in Zhejiang Province to collect cocoons should first register with the Zhejiang Provincial Sericulture Control Committee and will be allowed to freely purchase cocoons after approval.

Loan of 160,000 Yuan 117

Silk manufacturers in various counties in Zhejiang who want to improve machinery, etc. may apply for a loan from the Sericulture Control Committee, and the Sericulture Control Committee will send technicians to guide the improvement. The Committee stipulates that the total amount of loans for silk factories in Zhejiang Province to improve machinery, etc. in 1936 is 160,000 yuan in national currency. The interest rate is particularly low, at 2% per annum. The purpose is to encourage silk manufacturers to improve machinery, so that the products are exquisite and can compete with foreign silk in the European and American markets.

Temporarily Suspending Loans for Collecting Cocoons 118

According to another source, the reporter from the New Sound News learned that the Zhejiang Sericulture Control Committee initially planned to borrow 30 million yuan from Shanghai-Hangzhou banks to purchase this year's Zhejiang spring cocoons, but later changed it to a loan of 10 million yuan. Now, because Shanghai-Hangzhou banks' supply of caustic soda depends entirely on imports, since the establishment of Tianyuan Electrochemical Plant, which uses electrolysis to manufacture acids and alkalis, has given the industrial world a new look. In recent years, mass production has been able to fully supply domestic needs. Recently, with its surplus capacity, after much research and experimentation, a pure hydrochloric acid has been produced, which is so-called chemically pure. This pure hydrochloric acid is divided into two types, specific gravity 1.19 and 1.16, for chemical analysis and medicinal use. The manufacturing process is very cumbersome because it is necessary to remove extremely small amounts of impurities. The pure hydrochloric acid with a specific gravity of 1.19 is called fuming pure hydrochloric acid, and it is even more difficult to manufacture. There are only a handful of factories in the world that manufacture this type of hydrochloric acid, and even the United States does not have this product, so its high value can be seen. Scientific circles in Shanghai, such as the Industrial Chemistry Research Institute and the Shanghai Testing Laboratory established by foreigners, were the first to adopt it and were very satisfied. Special certificates have been issued. The Military Medical Department of the Military Affairs Committee and the National Health Administration have recently purchased a large amount of pure hydrochloric acid for medical use. Other organizations, such as the Construction Committee, the Zhejiang Construction Department, the National Central Research Institute, the Chemical Research Institute, the National Zhejiang University, and the Guizhou Construction Department, have also purchased it successively. The factory's manufacture of this type of pure hydrochloric acid is entirely a scientific contribution and does not take cost into account, so the price is very low.

Chairman's Report 122

The chairman reported the purpose of the meeting, and committee member Jue Shanxing reported on Mr. Deng's brief history and commemorative significance, briefly stating that today is the 14th anniversary of Mr. Deng Zhongyuan's martyrdom. Mr. Deng had revolutionary ideas since he was a child. At the age of 22, he graduated from the Jiangbian Zhaotang, which was the beginning of his revolutionary actions. One year before the Republic of China, the Wuhan Uprising occurred, and Mr. Deng gathered comrades in Guangdong to respond. After the success, Hu Zhantang was appointed Governor of Guangdong, and Mr. Deng was appointed Director of the Army Department. Later, the Governor's Office was reorganized, and he was appointed Garrison Commander of Qiongya. In addition to training troops, he devoted himself to construction. He soon resigned and went to Japan to assist the Prime Minister in organizing the Chinese Revolutionary Party and planning the campaign against Yuan. When Chen Jiongming rebelled, Mr. Deng was finally taken advantage of by villains. On March 21st of the 11th year, he returned to Guangdong from Hong Kong and was attacked by an assassin at the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway Station, being shot twice. He passed away at 5 a.m. on the 23rd, at the age of 38. Today, in commemorating Mr. Deng, there are several points that should be followed by us: We should follow Mr. Deng's spirit of not fearing death and not compromising; We should follow Mr. Deng's spirit of loving the Party and the country; We should follow Mr. Deng's spirit of studying knowledge and skills; We should follow Mr. Deng's spirit of integrity and thrift, etc. Then he shouted slogans and the meeting adjourned.

Suspension of Work Due to Lack of Raw Materials 125

After the recovery of foreign sales of Chinese silk, silk factories in Zhejiang, Shanghai, Wuxi, and other places started work one after another. Taking Shanghai as an example, there were more than 30 factories in total. However, due to the lack of raw materials, they successively suspended work. Now, only Baotai Silk Factory in Nanshi and a few other factories are still reeling silk. In addition, there is only one Folun Shuang Gong Silk Factory in Hongkou. It is heard that there are only a thousand dan or so of cocoons in stock in Zhejiang, Shanghai, and Wuxi. It is expected that all of them will be shut down soon, and work will not resume until the spring cocoons come on the market.

Lin Jinyu from the Auditing Department, Ye Zhendong from the Jiangsu Provincial Government, Chen Bilin from the Zhejiang Provincial Government (Xu Xibao as proxy), Qin Runqing from the Fund Management Committee, Li Fusun from the Bankers Association, Qin Xieqing from the Money Industry Association, Jin Wenyuan from the Central Bank, Cao Zhenzhao from the Bank of China, Chen Jun from the Bank of Communications, Jin Boming from the Zhejiang Local Bank, Zai Songqi from the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, Jin Wenwei from the Wing Hang Bank, Liu Taishi from the Jiangsu Bank, and more than 20 other people attended. Qin Runqing chaired the meeting and drew six ballots, with a principal of 180,000 yuan to be repaid. The winning bond tickets were scheduled to be paid by the Central and other six banks starting on the 31st of this month. The details are as follows:

Chairman's Report 127

After the rituals were performed, Chairman Runqing reported, briefly stating that today is the date for the 14th repayment drawing of the short-term public bonds of the Jiang-Zhejiang silk industry in the 21st year. We are very pleased to have you here to supervise and observe. A total of six ballots will be drawn for this repayment, with a principal of 180,000 yuan to be repaid. All winning bond tickets will be paid in cash by the Central, China, Communications, National Goods, Jiangsu, and Hangzhou Zhejiang Local Banks starting on the 31st of this month. Please check the ballot tickets and the ballot ticket registers so that the drawing can be carried out.

Winning Numbers 128

After the Chairman finished his report, the supervisors checked the ballots and the ballot ticket registers, and then the drawing was carried out. A total of six ballots were drawn, and the winning numbers are as follows: No. "28", No. "36", No. "48", No. "52", No. "83", No. "91", with a total repayment of 180,000 yuan. The above winning numbers were immediately entered into the register by the registration staff and announced on the bulletin board. The meeting adjourned at 10:30 a.m.

Guangdong Province Approves Reduction of Bran Tax 129

The Guangdong Provincial Government has reduced the bran tax on bran-based goods to 15 cents per dan. The Grain and Oilseed Industry Association and the Oilseed Industry Association, along with transportation companies across the country, have appealed to the central government for a reduction. They threatened strike and work stoppage until a compromise was reached after months of appealing. The Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry instructed the Guangdong Finance Commissioner's Office to lower the tax to alleviate merchant hardship. The Grain Industry Association of this city received Order No. 75 from the Guangdong Provincial Special Commissioner's Office, which reads: The Grain and Oilseed Industry Association and the Oilseed Industry Association of Shanghai City submitted a document on March 3, 1936, requesting the abolition of the additional tax on domestic bran for the construction of Zhongda (Central) University. The order approved, stating that the Southwest Political Affairs Committee of the National Government has ordered that the tax on domestic bran be reduced to 15 cents per dan. Except for special orders, you should comply with this order. The association notified the local industry. The bran tax dispute, which had lasted for half a year, came to an end.

German Ambassador to China, Dr. Trautmann, Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday 130

Returning Home Today by Ship Is Purely a Vacation; Rumors of Trautmann's Transfer Are Absolutely Untrue. Dr. Trautmann, the German Ambassador to China, who was originally scheduled to arrive in Shanghai on the evening of the 21st, had his trip postponed by one day due to some matter. He arrived in Shanghai at around 7:00 AM yesterday, accompanied by his wife and daughter, on the 11:00 PM express train from Beijing. The German Consul-General in Shanghai, Mr. Kriebel, and Consul Mr. Bienert, personally went to the North Station to welcome him. After alighting from the train, Ambassador Trautmann immediately transferred to a car and went directly to the Cathay Hotel on the Bund, Nanjing Road, to rest. Today, he and his wife will depart for home on the Norddeutscher Lloyd ship "Scharnhorst." The ship arrived in Shanghai yesterday afternoon from Japan and is docked between buoys number 11 and 12 in the Huangpu River. It is scheduled to depart from Shanghai at 4:00 PM today. Ambassador Trautmann has been in China for many years and has never returned home, so he has decided to make a special trip home. This is purely a vacation and he is scheduled to return to his post in November of this year after an eight-month holiday. There are rumors that Ambassador Trautmann will be ordered to take up a new post and will not return to China, and that Consul-General Kriebel in Shanghai will succeed him as Ambassador. However, according to the "New Voice" reporter's inquiries from semi-official German sources, this is pure speculation and is absolutely untrue.

The Telephone Company Sends Another Letter to the Taxpayers' Association, Protesting Specific Measures 133

Demanding the Abolition of the Limitation on Basic Calls and Advocating a Uniform Rate of Three Cents per Call.

The Special Zone Telephone Problem Committee sent another letter to the Chinese Ratepayers' Association in the Concession yesterday, suggesting measures to protest the telephone rate increase. The original letter reads: "Dear Sirs, We received your letter stating that you have decided to convene a temporary executive committee meeting on the 25th of this month to discuss how to deal with the telephone rate increase, which shows your concern for the public interest. We are very pleased. As the meeting is imminent, we are now listing again the reasons why the company's rate increase is unreasonable, and request that this be raised for discussion at the meeting. Telephone is a public utility with the aim of facilitating the people, and should never be treated as a commercial profit-making entity. Since the Shanghai Telephone Company took over in 1928, the annual surplus has always been hundreds of thousands or more. The company is upgrading equipment to accommodate 200,000 telephones. Currently, only 46,000 telephones are installed in the city. Therefore, the burden of 200,000 telephones is being distributed among 46,000 users, resulting in the current rate increase. We believe that this kind of measure, which is contrary to economics, is tantamount to extorting the city's economy. Once this precedent is set, rates can be increased at any time as the number of users decreases. The company currently charges 6.5 yuan per month for residential telephones, limited to 100 calls, and 10 yuan per month for business telephones, limited to 150 calls. Each additional call is charged at 3 cents. Based on 100 calls for residential telephones, the value of each call is 6.5 cents. Based on 150 calls for business telephones, the value of each call is a little over 6.2 cents. The same telephone equipment is subject to two different charging methods. Since you have already stipulated the charging method for each additional call, we hereby request that your association advocate that the Shanghai Telephone Company's charging method should be uniformly calculated at 3 cents per call, which is fair. If the above objective cannot be achieved, we are willing to sacrifice everything to deal with it. National economy, we urge you to persist and strive..."

The Ratepayers' Association Sends a Letter to the French Municipal Council, Requesting Exemption from Illegal Donations and Licenses 135

The Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the French Concession sent a letter to the French Municipal Council yesterday regarding the forced donation of members of the Second District and Second Branch of the Municipal Federation. The letter reads: "Dear Sirs, Mr. [illegible] of the Dongxinqiao Street Yeziting Shengyi Daxing [illegible] Tea and Food Store on Fada Road, a member of our association, has sent a letter stating that his store has been open for more than ten years. He has already obtained the business donation license from the French Municipal Council in accordance with the regulations. Unexpectedly, investigators from the Hygiene Bureau came for the past two days and said that another hygiene license is required for the internal operations, and that an investigation fee of ten yuan must be paid first." According to regulations, a factory scale must have more than five workers and not be listed in the classification before taxes can be levied. Most of the goods in the store are wholesale from candy companies, and a small number of pastries are made by one or two workers. There is no factory scale, and a classified business has already been donated. Furthermore, there are donation tickets that can be verified. Therefore, we are sending this letter to your council to request immediate negotiations to avoid unnecessary losses for merchants. According to this, since the store's business donation license has already been obtained in accordance with regulations, and the pastry-making factory does not have a factory scale, there is no reason to levy donations according to regulations. In view of the aforementioned circumstances, we hereby request that your council immediately order the Hygiene Bureau to exempt the store from factory donations and taxes in order to be considerate of the difficulties of merchants. Sincerely, the Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the French Concession, Shanghai French Concession."

Overseas Chinese Merchants in Batavia Send a Letter Reporting That the Dutch East Indies Offers Preferential Treatment for Imports of Chinese Goods. 136

Extra Imports Allowed Without Restrictions; Import Tariffs on National Goods Are the Same as for All Countries.

The Shanghai National Products Factory Federation received a letter from the Overseas Chinese Importers Association of Batavia, Dutch East Indies, which stated: "Dear Sirs, According to the items discussed at the first regular meeting of the second year of our association on the 6th of this month, after the Dutch East Indies government restricted the import of goods from various countries, the Import Bureau of the Ministry of Economic Affairs gave special preferential treatment to formal import merchants importing Chinese goods, allowing extra imports. However, according to reports in domestic newspapers, there are various difficulties in importing various national goods into the Dutch East Indies, which do not correspond to the facts. The current situation of national goods imports here can be divided into three categories: 1. National goods imported into the Dutch East Indies that have not been restricted can be imported freely (the same as before). 2. National goods that have been listed as restricted can still obtain an extra special import permit in addition to the regular permit (this permit is limited to formal import merchants and those with export evidence). 3. Import tariffs on national goods are the same as for all countries, and there are no exceptions or difficulties. It was decided to send separate letters to various chambers of commerce and factory associations in China to inform them of the import situation of national goods here in order to clarify rumors and benefit national goods. In addition to sending separate letters, we hereby inform you for your information in order to correct rumors and benefit national goods. Sincerely, Qiu Yuanrong, Chairman of the Overseas Chinese Importers Association of the Dutch East Indies, Zhuang Xiyan, General Affairs."

Sending a Letter to the Municipal Federation Requesting That All Public Organizations Unite to Proceed.

The original letter reads: "Dear Sirs, We have read in the newspaper that the political department of the French Concession police summoned representatives of various hotel industries within the Concession on the 11th of this month to discuss the collection of aviation national salvation donations by our government, and ordered them to stop, and even imposed fines. At the same time, similar incidents occurred in the Public Concession. The news has spread and is infuriating. Before a satisfactory resolution is reached, notify the citizens of the two Special Zones to stop paying taxes. 5. If necessary, make a strong representation to prompt the Concession authorities to reflect. The matter concerns national survival and the people's voluntary patriotic efforts. We urge you to convene a representative conference of all districts as soon as possible to discuss the overall plan and then unite all public organizations in the city to proceed together. Time is of the essence, do not delay."

Chinese Steamer Sinks Two Barges in the Huangpu River 140

Five Boatmen Drowned

A certain Fuzhou-bound steamer of a certain Chinese merchant-run shipping company in Shanghai, loaded with goods and passengers from Nantai, Fujian, was entering the port at around 9:00 AM the day before yesterday. When the steamer reached the Huangpu River near Yangshupu, due to the strong tide and wind, as the steamer was proceeding forward, two cargo barges happened to be coming head-on. The steamer tried to avoid them but was unable to do so, causing the bow of the steamer to violently hit the two barges. They immediately cracked, water entered the barges, and they overturned and sank at the same time. The goods on the two barges also sank into the Huangpu River. The boatmen, including the captain of the barges, who were unable to escape in time, also fell into the river. Fortunately, nearby civilian boats and small boats rushed to the scene to help with the rescue, rescuing some of the boatmen who had fallen into the water. As a result, five people could not be retrieved, presumably swept away by the turbulent water and drowned. The bodies have not yet been recovered. The barge owners are investigating the losses and preparing to negotiate with the shipping company for compensation. The Chinese steamer continued on its way as usual.

Ningbo Industrial Bank's Restoration Preparatory Office to Close at the End of the Month 143

Scheduled to Reopen

After the Ningbo Industrial Bank temporarily suspended accepting settlements, the bank's creditors, together with fellow Ningbo natives, organized the Ningbo Industrial Bank Restoration Preparatory Office to carry out the restoration work. The work has been progressing very smoothly. In accordance with the restoration plan, repayments have been made to depositors, reaching more than 90% of the total debt. However, there are still a small number of depositors whose addresses are unknown or who have moved without notifying, so the office has been unable to contact them. It has recently been learned that the office has received instructions from the Ministry of Finance to reopen the bank within a specified time. It has been decided that those depositors who have not yet completed the procedures at the office must do so by the end of this month. Those who fail to do so by the deadline will be reported to the Ministry for record. After the bank reopens, these few depositors must still follow the restoration procedures in order to avoid any discrepancies, so that the interests of all creditors can be protected and social finance can be stabilized.

Aviation Association Orders Trainer Aircraft; One Completed and Test Flight Today 144

At Approximately 4:00 PM at the Longhua Airfield; Piloted by Instructor Xu Chengqi of the Aircraft Office.

The China Aviation Commission, in order to provide flying practice for members of the Flying Club, specially ordered three trainer aircraft from the Aircraft Manufacturing Office of the Ministry of the Navy. The first aircraft has been completed, and it is scheduled to have instructor Xu Chengqi from the office pilot a test flight. Details are as follows:

New Aircraft Design. A New Voice reporter visited the Naval Aircraft Office yesterday to see the new aircraft. The aircraft is a biplane amphibious trainer. The fuselage is cyan-yellow, and the wings are silver-grey. The total weight is 1,600 pounds. There are two seats in the front and rear. According to Zeng Yijing, director of the office, the cost is 16,000 yuan and it took ten days to build. All materials used in the aircraft, except for the engine, which was purchased from the United States, such as metal, magnetic paint, cedar, and other miscellaneous materials, are made in China. Therefore, it is no less than a domestically produced aircraft.

Test Flight Today. Most of the aircraft's construction has been completed. Yesterday, Zeng Yijing was supervising the assembly by the engineering staff. It is expected to be completed this morning. It is scheduled to be piloted by Xu Chengqi, an instructor from the office, at approximately 4:00 PM today, from the Jiangmian airport to the Longhua airport for a test flight. At that time, members of the Chinese Flying Club will go to Longhua airport to watch the test flight. After the test flight, the aircraft will be handed over to the Aviation Association for use by the Flying Club members.

Special Zone Rickshaw Association to Convene a Car Owner Congress on the 27th 145

To Discuss Measures to Reduce Rickshaw Rental Fees.

The Special Zone Rickshaw Association will convene a car owner congress on the 27th to discuss countermeasures because the Municipal Council plans to implement a reduction in rickshaw rental fees starting on April 1. Yesterday, a notice was sent to the car merchants, stating: "This is to notify you that the Public Concession Rickshaw Affairs Committee is a redundant organ of the Police Department. Since its establishment, its various measures, such as forcibly reducing rickshaw rental fees, forcing the replacement of new rickshaw models, restricting rickshaw puller registration, charging each person one yuan, and forcibly donating rickshaw puller mutual aid fees of seven cents per vehicle per day, are all intended to put the car merchants and rickshaw pullers to death. Although the association has negotiated, fortunately, the Municipal Council authorities have understood and have entered into agreements with the association, such as the regulations on rickshaw rental fees of 85 cents per day on August 6, 1934, and the unrestricted rickshaw puller registration on November 23. These have temporarily maintained the status quo of the rickshaw industry, which supports more than 300,000 poor Chinese in the Concession. Unfortunately, the Car Committee, due to the approaching end of its term, has intensified its efforts and has disregarded all agreements and suggested to the Municipal Council that rental fees be reduced by eight cents starting on April 1, arbitrarily restricting rickshaw pullers from earning a living, resulting in more than 20,000 unemployed people. Vehicles are parked daily, and donations and mutual aid fees must still be paid. At a time when the market is sluggish and the prices of rickshaw materials are soaring, the impact on the rickshaw industry is profound and significant. As for the rickshaw pullers who are unemployed due to the Car Committee's refusal to register them, they are still responsible for maintaining their livelihoods, and they are all exhausted. In order to save the livelihoods of our colleagues in the city, it has been decided to hold a special zone car owner congress in the auditorium of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce on North Henan Road at 9:00 AM on March 27 to discuss all measures to carry out the rescue. We hope that all car owners will actively participate and attend."
